himself to death as 200 4Chan viewers egged him on</h1><ul><li><span style="font-weight: bold;"><font style="font-size: 1.4em;">A 20-year-old man studying at Ontario's University of Guelph tried to kill himself live on 4chan <br /></font></span></li><li><span style="font-weight: bold;"><font style="font-size: 1.4em;">4chan is an imageboard website allowing users to post anonymously</font></span></li><li><span style="font-weight: bold;"><font style="font-size: 1.4em;">'Stephen' lit a fire as 200 people watched on a live video stream</font></span></li><li><span style="font-weight: bold;"><font style="font-size: 1.4em;">Footage shows him being pulled out by firefighters</font></span></li><li><span style="font-weight: bold;"><font style="font-size: 1.4em;">The student is in a serious but non-life threatening condition with his devastated mother at his bedside <br /></font></span></li><li><span style=" font-weight: bold;"><font style=" font-size: 1.4em;">The University is now trying to stop fellow students watching the live footage</font></span></li></ul> <p class="author-section byline-plain">By  <a an online messageboard. <br /></font></p><p><font style="font-size:1.2em;">The 20-year-old, who identified himself only as 'Stephen', announced on the anonymous 4chan website that he intended to commit suicide and broadcast the event for others to see.</font></p><p><font style="font-size:1.2em;">Disturbingly, scores of online users signed up to watch the suicide attempt and helped the man to set up the video stream for the 'an hero' - online slang for suicide attempt. <br /></font></p><div class="clear"> </div><div class="artSplitter"> including famously Sarah Palin's private email<br /></font></p><p><font style="font-size: 1.2em;">The /b/ board is said to be the most popular page on the site and coincidentally home to its most sickening material<br /></font></p><p><font style="font-size: 1.2em;">It often includes pornography and vicious bullying<br /></font></p><p><font style="font-size: 1.2em;">The term 'an hero' - used to discuss suicide on the site - is a good example of how vile users can become<br /></font></p><p><font style="font-size: 1.2em;">  Spotting a grammatical error on the memorial page for seventh  grader <a style="font-weight:bold;" target="_blank" rel="nofollow" href="http://www.nytimes.com/2008/08/03/magazine/03trolls-t.html?pagewanted=all">Mitchell Henderson</a>, who shot himself in the head with his parents'  rifle in 2008, 4chan users thought the typo more worthy of interest than the tragic death<br /></font></p><p><font style="font-size: 1.2em;">They began to bombard the boards with images and messages mocking Mitchell's death and the people mourning him which even led to prank phone calls being made to his parents <br /></font></p><p><font style="font-size:1.2em;">Several other bullying victims and mourning families have complained of similar treatment by the site</font></p><p><font style="font-size:1.2em;"><a style="font-weight:bold;" target="_blank" rel="nofollow" href="http://www.dailydot.com/news/4chan-hannah-smith-suicide-facebook-trolls/">Hannah Smith</a> who killed herself after months of cyber-bullying was one such victim as was <a style="font-weight:bold;" target="_blank" rel="nofollow" href="http://www.dailymail.co.uk/news/article-1360788/Natasha-MacBryde-suicide-Vile-web-craze-taunted-family-bullied-girl-death.html">Natasha MacBryde</a><br /></font></p><p><font style="font-size:1.2em;">The site can at times claim responsibility for some good deeds. On  one occasion the community tracked down a man who posted videos of  alleged cat abuse which led to his arrest</font></p></div></div> <p><font style="font-size:1.2em;">She added: âA fire was reported at 7.40 on Saturday evening and fire and police responded. The fire was put out and they found the injured student.</font></p><p><font style="font-size:1.2em;">âThe damage was confined to the studentâs residence but students were evacuated as a precaution. <br /></font></p><p><font style="font-size:1.2em;">'We were suspicious the fire had been started by the student but the police began investigating. <br /></font></p><p><font style="font-size:1.2em;">'When videos started circulating yesterday (Sunday) meetings were called with university staff and students and counsellors brought in to be available to any students as obviously itâs a disturbing situation. <br /></font></p><p><font style="font-size:1.2em;">âWe are also advising students not to watch or share the video. Weâre trying to take it down but itâs on so many guerrilla sites itâs almost impossible to do that.â</font></p><p><font style="font-size:1.2em;">Brenda White</font><span style="font-size: 1.2em;">side, Associate Vice President for Student Affairs told MailOnline: âWe havenât been able to speak to the student yet. Heâs in hospital and heâs going to be okay.Â </span></p><p></p><p><font style="font-size:1.2em;">'He canât talk to anyone at the moment. His mum is with him and we may be able to talk to him in the next day or two. Heâs going to be in a fragile state. Weâre respecting his privacy and need to recover with the interest itâs a difficult balance.'<br /></font></p><p><font style="font-size:1.2em;"> According to the <a </font><font style="font-size:1.2em;">rushed to hospital with 'serious but non life-threatening injuries' caused by smoke inhalation.</font></p><p><font style="font-size:1.2em;">Two staff members were also taken to hospital but were later released. <br /></font></p><p><font style="font-size:1.2em;">120 students were evacuated and 42 remain out of their rooms as the investigation continues.<br
